      <h3>UC Riverside Identity Standards Online Manual</h3> 
      <h4 class="version">(Version 2-10-10)</h4> 
      <p class="kicker"> The University of California, Riverside (UCR) is one of 10 universities within the prestigious University of California system, and the only UC located in Inland Southern California. To convey an image consistent with who we are and to communicate effectively with many diverse constituents and key stakeholders, UCR has established a unified institutional brand and marketing program. </p> 
      <h4>Why a Unified Identity?</h4> 
      <p> The goal of unified branding, as described in this manual and instituted through the integrated marketing program, is to represent our shared identity through an easily-remembered positive public image. A consistent, unified brand significantly enhances the coordination of our campus communications efforts, conveying a professional and positive image to our valued constituencies. A unified brand that is attractive and well represents our institution is more effective at competing in a crowded marketplace for new students, faculty and funding resources. </p> 
      <h4>You Benefit from a Single Reference</h4> 
      <p> The UC Riverside Identity Standards Manual, sometimes referred to as the &quot;style guide&quot;, was developed by the UCR Office of Strategic Communications in conjunction with stakeholders and senior management across campus. This manual is the official reference and provides guidelines for all campus colleges, departments and units, and is intended to help anyone who writes, edits or designs printed, electronic, or other publications and materials for and about UCR. Easy and economical to implement, the manual is useful for a variety of formats and applications, with a flexibility that allows campus units to retain their individuality and capitalize on the benefits of a unified UCR brand. Consistent use of this manual will ensure that UC and UCR policies and guidelines are being properly applied to official stationery, business cards, signage, university web sites, the seal, products, publications and collateral materials. </p> 
      <div class="column23 nota-bene"> 
       <h4> If you have questions or need help, please contact the following: </h4> 
       <address> <strong>UCR Office of Strategic Communications</strong><br /> General Information or Referral: (951) 827-6397<br /> Marketing: (951) 827-2494<br /> Creative Design Services: (951) 827-7178 </address> 
      </div>

             <div id="watch-description" class="yt-uix-expander yt-uix-expander-collapsed yt-uix-button-panel"> 
              <div id="watch-description-content"> 
               <div id="watch-description-clip"> 
                <p id="watch-uploader-info"> <strong>Published on <span id="eow-date" class="watch-video-date">Mar 5, 2014</span> </strong> </p> 
                <div id="watch-description-text"> 
                 <p id="eow-description">Big hair, big moves — in the 1980s, the University of California had an average population of about 5,000 people. (These days, that's the population of ONE graduating class.) Check out more stories of what it was like to be at UCR in the 1980s at in the Winter 2014 issue of UCR Magazine. <br /><br /><a href="http://magazine.ucr.edu" target="_blank" title="http://magazine.ucr.edu" rel="nofollow" dir="ltr" class="yt-uix-redirect-link">http://magazine.ucr.edu</a></p> 
                </div>

     <div id="omnicontent"> 
      <!-- com.omniupdate.div label="home-image" group="Everyone" button="657" -->
      <!-- com.omniupdate.editor csspath="/z-omniupdate/css/style.css" cssmenu="/z-omniupdate/css/style.txt" width="484" -->
      <!-- /com.omniupdate.div --> 
      <!-- com.omniupdate.div label="maincontent" group="Everyone" button="657" -->
      <!-- com.omniupdate.editor csspath="/z-omniupdate/css/style.css" cssmenu="/z-omniupdate/css/style.txt" width="484" -->
      <p>IBM's RACF security package operates on the IBM mainframe. RACF access to data is granted on a need-to-know basis; requests for data access must be made in writing to Administrative Computing.</p> 
      <p>RACF utilizes a combination of userid and password to control who can access what resources and how and when those resources can be accessed.</p> 
      <h3>Rules</h3> 
      <ul> 
       <li><a href="/change_password_freq.html">Change your password frequently</a>; change it immediately if you suspect that it is no longer secret.</li> 
       <li>Do not write the password down or leave it for others to see.</li> 
       <li>Do not share USERID's or passwords. Every person using the IBM mainframe must have their own unique USERID and password. Individuals are held responsible and accountable for everything done with their USERID.</li> 
       <li>Do not leave your work station while you are logged on. Log off if you are away from your desk.</li> 
       <li>Notify Administrative Computing immediately when an employee that has a USERID and password is transferred, terminated, or no longer has authorization to see the data.</li> 
       <li>USERID's with no activity for one year are automatically deleted.</li> 
       <li>A user may change passwords at any time, and frequent changes (such as weekly) give added protection against unauthorized access.</li> 
       <li>Our RACF requires that <a href="/change_password_freq.html">passwords be changed</a> at least once every 180 days. (RACF maintains a history of a USERID's twelve most recent passwords, which cannot be reused.)</li> 
      </ul> 
      <h3>Suspended USERID</h3> 
      <ul> 
       <li>If a USERID is &quot;suspended&quot; by RACF, IBM access will be denied.</li> 
       <li>To &quot;unsuspend&quot; a USERID or other password issues, users should contact the Security Administrator at x25938 -- you will be required to furnish proof of identity.</li> 
      </ul>
      <!-- /com.omniupdate.div -->
